<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">A low-profile radio frequency identification (RFID) tag antenna is proposed with a compact size of 45 ×45 mm<sup>2</sup> and circular polarization (CP) for metallic surfaces. A star-shaped slot is etched onto the antenna for the CP and antenna size reduction. A terminal-grounded L-shaped feedline is embedded in the etched slot to efficiently excite the wideband CP mode, complexly match the tag-antenna impedance, and further reduce the antenna size. The embedded feed structure also helps achieve a relatively higher gain, resulting in a longer reading range. The proposed antenna can cover the impedance bandwidth of 60 MHz (from 880 to 940 MHz) as well as the 3-dB CP bandwidth of 12 MHz (from 905 to 917 MHz). Further results demonstrate that the proposed tag antenna provides a stable reading range when mounted on metal plates of various sizes.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>In Modern times, the technology of passive ultrahigh frequency (UHF) radio frequency identification (RFID) has been applied in many fields, such as assets management, retail industry, and manufacturing. Nowadays, RFID tag antennas with circular polarization (CP) radiation have drawn much attention. The reason for this is that the overwhelming majority of reader antennas are designed with CP, which causes a polarization mismatch between the reader and tag antenna if the tag antenna uses linear polarization (LP) such as in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. The polarization mismatch causes an unwanted decrease in the reading range. Thus, the reading range can be improved if we use a CP tag antenna with the same handedness as a CP reader antenna. In addition, commercial sectors propose a growing demand that the tag antennas are mountable on metallic surfaces. Therefore, it is very necessary to design RFID tag antennas with circular polarization and the ability to be mounted on metallic surfaces.</p><p>To conquer the challenges mentioned above, many works have been carried out during the past years <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. Some metal-mountable LP tag antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a> and non-metal-mountable CP tag antennas <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> have been proposed. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, some metal-mountable CP tag antennas have been published, and good feed methods are provided to achieve CP radiation. However, the feeding structures of these designs have to occupy some additional areas outside the radiators. This will increase the overall size of the tag antennas. Here, the definition of the overall size is the size of antenna top-layer metallization (including the radiator patch and the feeding network). Moreover, these external feed networks create asymmetries in the shapes of tag antennas. This results in a reduction of the antenna gain in the boresight direction. In addition, the designs in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a> have a relatively narrow 3-dB axial-ratio (AR) bandwidth of 6 MHz, which is not desired in practical applications. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, an RFID reader antenna with a feed network embedded in the slot is proposed to achieve CP radiation and a relatively wider CP bandwidth of 12 MHz. However, it is matched to 50 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-3" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and the thickness of the reader antenna is over 10 mm, which is not suitable for RFID tag antennas.</p><p>In this letter, a compact low-profile CP RFID tag antenna is proposed for metallic objects. A star-shaped slot modified from <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a> is etched on the tag antenna, which could provide a wideband CP mode. In order to efficiently excite this wideband CP mode in the low-profile tag antenna, a terminal-grounded L-shaped feedline is embedded in the etched slot. By optimizing the geometries of the slot and feedline, a wider CP bandwidth of 12 MHz (from 905 to 917 MHz) is achieved compared to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. This embedded feed network can also fulfill the complex impedance matching between the antenna and chip. Furthermore, the embedded feed solution will help the tag antenna form a symmetrical radiating structure to realize a more compact size and higher gain as opposed to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. The investigated and experimentally verified results will be presented when the tag antenna is in free space or mounted on metallic surfaces.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Structure and Design</h2></div><p>The configuration of the proposed tag antenna and the corresponding photograph of the prototype are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. An asymmetric star-shaped slot is etched on a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math" style="width: 6.309em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.649em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1005.65em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">45</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">45</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.99em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.985em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">45\times 45{\hbox{-mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> radiating patch to produce the CP and reduce the antenna size. The grooved patch is mounted onto a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-18" role="math" style="width: 6.309em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.649em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1005.65em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-20" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">70</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">70</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.99em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-25"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.985em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">70\times 70{\hbox{-mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> ground plane. The operating band of the antenna is tuned to 902–928 MHz. The substrate between the radiating patch and ground plane is a low-cost FR4 printed circuit board (PCB) with a thickness of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-32" role="math" style="width: 3.907em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.486em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.25em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-33"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-34"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-35"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-37" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-38" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1.6</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-39" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">{h}=1.6~</script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm, relative permittivity of 4.4, and loss tangent of 0.02. A terminal-grounded L-shaped microstrip feedline, with a coupled distance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-40" role="math" style="width: 3.306em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.946em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.71em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-41"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-42"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-43"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-44" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-45" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-46" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-47" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">{D}=1~</script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm away from the slot edge, is embedded in the star-shaped slot to capacitively excite the grooved patch. The width of the slot branches with and without the feedline are 3.7 and 3 mm, respectively. The microstrip feedline can also help match the impedance of the welded Monza4 tag chip (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-48" role="math" style="width: 5.649em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.048em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.99em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-49"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-50" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-51" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-52" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-53"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-54" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">j</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-55" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">143</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-56" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-57" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">11-{\rm j}143~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 911 MHz, threshold power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-58" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.589em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1005.35em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-59"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-60"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-61"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-62"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-63" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-64"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-65"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-66" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-67" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">h</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-68" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-69" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-70" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">17.4</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-71" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">{P}_{\rm th} =-17.4~</script></tex-math></inline-formula>dBm). In order to achieve the greatest transmission energy from the chip to the antenna, the complex impedance of the antenna should be set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-72" role="math" style="width: 5.649em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.048em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.99em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-73"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-74" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-75" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-76" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-77"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-78" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">j</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-79" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">143</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-80" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-81" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">11+{\rm j}143~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig>Geometries and the prototype of the proposed compact circularly polarized patch tag antenna (unit: millimeters).</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6843861/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>First, in view of the short-circuited transmission line theory from <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>, the total short-circuited length of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-82" role="math" style="width: 4.688em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.207em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.09em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-83"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-84" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-85"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-86"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-87"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-88" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-89"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-90"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-91" style="font-size: 70.7%; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-216"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-217" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-218" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">11+143~{\rm j}\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at 911 MHz. Then, we make the antenna and chip conjugate impedance matching with each other. The detailed dimensions of the designed antenna are shown in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig>Measured and simulated input impedances of the proposed tag antenna.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6843861/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Results and Discussions</h2></div><p>In this letter, all the simulations are carried out with the ANSYS HFSS. The concept of power reflection coefficient (PRC) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-225" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.31em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-226"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-227" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Γ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-228" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&lt;</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-229" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-230" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-231" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.13em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">\Gamma&lt; -3~</script></tex-math></inline-formula>dB <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_3">[12]</a> is introduced to define the impedance bandwidth of our RFID tag antenna. With the method in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_3">[13]</a>, the input impedances are successfully measured by the four-port vector network analyzer (VNA) (Agilent N5247A) and a test fixture. The measured and simulated input impedances of our proposed tag antenna are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. The corresponding PRC chart is provided in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>. The measured and the simulated results agree well with each other. The specified 3-dB PRC bandwidth of our antenna is 60 MHz (from 880 to 940 MHz), which completely meets the 902–928-MHz band requirement.</p><p>In the following, we will provide the analysis of realizing a broad CP bandwidth by tuning the length of the feedline and star-shaped slot. The length of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-232" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-233"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-234"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-235"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-236"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-237" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-238"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-239"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-240" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">{L}_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>] is approximately equivalent to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-241" role="math" style="width: 16.279em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-247"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-248"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-249" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-250" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-251" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">λ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-252"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-253"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-254" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-255" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">6</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-256" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-257" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-258"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-262"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-263"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-264" style="font-size: 70.7%; padding-left: 0.183em;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-275"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">{L}_{2}+ \lambda/6~({L}_{1} =32.3~{\hbox{mm}},~{L}_{2} =5~</script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm). A phase delay is induced by the L-shaped capacitive-coupled feedline in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, and then two orthogonal fields contributing to CP can be excited. To put two resonant modes around 911 MHz, the slot length of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-285" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.96em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-286"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-287"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>, condition 1 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-320" role="math" style="width: 14.237em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-363"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-364"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-365" style="font-size: 70.7%; The corresponding AR bandwidth diagram is exhibited in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. As we can see from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(b)</a>, under condition 1, two resonant modes are in the vicinity of the 911-MHz band so that there is a wave in the phase difference portrait. However, the two resonant modes could not be put together when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-402" role="math" style="width: 3.667em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.31em 2.526em -999.997em); As a result, under constrain of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-419" role="math" style="width: 3.667em; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-422"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-423"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-424" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-425"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-426"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-427" style="font-size: 70.7%; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-433"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-434"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-435" style="font-size: 70.7%; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-27">{\rm S}_{1} &lt; {\rm S}_{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, a wide AR bandwidth of 12 MHz will be obtained after optimization.

<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig>Simulated axial ratio of the antenna.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6843861/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>We only present the simulated radiation patterns at 911 MHz in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 6</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">7</a> because of the current technical restriction. According to the simulated normalized CP gain radiation patterns plotted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>, our antenna possesses a 3-dB beamwidth of about 76° and a good front-to-back radiation ratio of around 24 dB in both the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-30-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-454" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-455"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-456" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-457" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-30">xz</script></tex-math></inline-formula>- and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-31-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-458" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.96em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-459"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-460" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-461" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-31">yz</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-planes, which indicates an excellent and pure right-hand circular polarization (RHCP) radiation when it is placed in free space. Likewise, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> presents the simulated gain radiation patterns at 911 MHz when it is placed on a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-32-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-462" role="math" style="width: 7.39em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.67em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1006.67em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-463"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-464" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">400</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-465" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-466" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">400</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-467"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.99em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-468"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-469"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-470"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-471"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-472" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.985em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-473"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-474"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-475" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-32">400\times 400{\hbox{-mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> metallic surface. It demonstrates that the value of the difference between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-33-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-476" role="math" style="width: 1.264em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.14em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-477"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-478"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-479"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-480"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-481" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-482" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-33">{E}_\theta</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-483" role="math" style="width: 1.505em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.32em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-484"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-485"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-486"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-487"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-488" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">E<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-489" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">Φ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-34">{E}_\Phi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is within 1 dB in the boresight direction, which implies that our antenna maintains good CP radiation when it is mounted on metal plate.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig>Simulated normalized CP gain radiation patterns at 911 MHz.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6843861/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig>Simulated antenna realized gain patterns at 911 MHz on metal plate.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6843861/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> shows the simulated gains of our tag antenna in different placement environments (in free space, as well as mounted on metal plates of various sizes). In fact, as the figure reveals, the antenna gain will stably maintain around −8 dBic as long as the ground plane size is more than <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-490" role="math" style="width: 7.33em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.61em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1006.61em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-491"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-492" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">100</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-493" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-494" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">100</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-495" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-496"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-497"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-498"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-499"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-500"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-501" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-502"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-503"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-504" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-35">100\times 100~{\hbox{mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The antenna gain is improved by 5 dB when placed on the metal rather than in free space. A larger metal plate could enlarge the antenna current area, which may help to enhance the antenna gain. The simulated peak radiation efficiency is 5% in the whole operating frequency band. The poor radiation efficiency is caused by the compact size and the low profile of the antenna and is quite common when the thickness of the patch antenna is only 1.6 mm.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig>Simulated antenna realized gains.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6843861/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Comparison of Antenna Parameters Between Proposed Antenna and Antennas in [6]–[8]<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table II" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>To further illustrate the preponderance of our antenna compared to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3">[6]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a>, we will discuss in detail the differences of gain and AR bandwidth between our antenna (slightly optimized after the ground size changes) and the antenna of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3">[6]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a> in comparable cases. As we can see from <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>, our optimal antenna presents a higher gain, a wider AR bandwidth of 12 MHz as opposed to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3">[6]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3">[7]</a>, and a smaller radiator size, when using corresponding ground plane sizes equal to those in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3">[6]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_3">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a>. In addition, with a smaller ground plane of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-505" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.589em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1005.59em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-506"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-507" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">60</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-508" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-509" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">60</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-510" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-511"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-512"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-513"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-514"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-515"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-516" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-517"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-518"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-519" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">60\times 60~{\hbox{mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the proposed antenna can still achieve a gain of −14.9 dBic and AR bandwidth of 12 MHz. Note that the ground plane size is the size of the actual antenna ground plane joined to the top-layer metallization through shorting pins. Although the AR bandwidth of our antenna is smaller than in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a>, the broader AR bandwidth in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a> was achieved at the cost of a larger area of feed network and radiator. Moreover, after reasonably changing the overall size (the size of antenna top layer metallization) of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a> to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-520" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.589em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1005.59em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-521"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-522" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">58</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-523" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-524" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">58</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-525" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-526"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-527"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-528"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-529"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-530"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-531" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-532"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-533"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-534" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">58\times 58~{\hbox{mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the simulated optimized AR bandwidth of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3">[8]</a> will reduce to 8 MHz.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig>Measured reading distances when the tag antenna is rotated along the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-535" role="math" style="width: 0.863em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.665em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1000.6em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-536"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-537" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">φ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">\varphi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> direction with a fixed reader antenna.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6843861/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table III </b>Read Range Results of the Proposed Antenna and the Small LP Metal Mountable Tags [2], [3] With the Same Output Power (3.98 W) at the Operating Frequency<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6843861/6843861-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table III" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p><p>The read range results of our tag antenna, and the small LP metal-mountable tags <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_3">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_3">[3]</a> for comparison, are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a>. It is noted that the reader antenna type of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_3">[2]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_3">[3]</a> is not given. For better embodying the antenna performance and carrying out the measurement, two RFID reader antennas—an LP reader antenna (Laird-E9012PLNF, gain of 12 dBi) and a CP reader antenna (Laird A9028, gain of 8 dBi)—are attached respectively to an RFID reader module (IPJ R420) with operating frequencies of 902–928 MHz and the same equivalent isotropically radiated power of 3.98 W. The measured maximal reading distances of our tag antenna, in free space and on metal plates with two different areas <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-538" role="math" style="width: 16.339em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 14.718em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1014.6em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-539"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-540" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-541" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">100</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-542" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-543" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">100</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-544" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-545"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-546"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-547"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-548"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-549"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-550" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-551"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-552"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-553" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-554" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-555" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;"> </span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-556" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">400</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-557" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-558" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">400</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-559" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-560"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-561"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-562"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-563"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-564"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-565" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-566"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-567"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-568" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-569" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.337em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">(100\times 100~{\hbox{mm}}^{2},~ 400\times 400~{\hbox{mm}}^{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> when the tag antenna rotated along the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-570" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-571"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-572" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">φ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">\varphi</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-direction and the LP reader antenna fixed, are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>. In free space, the reading range presents similar distances in the vicinity of 1.5 m at all angle measures of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-573" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-574"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-575" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">φ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">\varphi</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In addition, when mounted on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-576" role="math" style="width: 7.39em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.67em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1006.67em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-577"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-578" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">400</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-579" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-580" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">400</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-581"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.405em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.99em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-582"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-583"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-584"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-585"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-586" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">-mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.985em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-587"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-588"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-589" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">400\times 400{\hbox{-mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> metal plates, it shows a stable read range changes between 2.74 to 3.35 m with varying values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-590" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.6em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-591"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-592" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">φ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">\varphi</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The reading distance will stay around 3 m only if the metal plate size is above <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-593" role="math" style="width: 7.33em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.61em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1006.61em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-594"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-595" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">100</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-596" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-597" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">100</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-598" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-599"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-600"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-601"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-602"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-603"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-604" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-605"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-606"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-607" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">100\times 100~{\hbox{mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Therefore, this result further shows the excellent characteristics of CP radiation and the reliable on-metal reading range of the proposed antenna. The stability of the on-metal read range is very practical. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a> gives all the measured and simulated reading distances within the local equivalent isotropic radiated power (EIRP) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3">[14]</a>. Here, we apply the Friis transmission formula <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_3">[4]</a> to calculate the theoretical reading distance. The results indicate that our tag antenna can give a reasonable read range when placed in the conditions of free space or on metal plates.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A compact RFID tag antenna with good CP bandwidth has been designed and tested. A good AR bandwidth of 12 MHz and compact radiator size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-608" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.589em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1005.59em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-609"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-610" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">45</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-611" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-612" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">45</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-613" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-614"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-615"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-616"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-617"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-618"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-619" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-620"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-621"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-622" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">45\times 45~{\hbox{mm}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are obtained by introducing the slot-embedded-coupling feed network with good impedance matching. Thanks to the compact and symmetrical radiator, our antenna has the potential to utilize a smaller ground plane and exhibits a relatively higher gain against other designs in fair conditions. Later simulations and experiments indicate a good performance of our antenna when mounted on metallic surfaces. Therefore, all these performances ensure the proposed UHF RFID tag antenna is a good candidate for the application of mounting on metallic surfaces.</p></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

A terminal-grounded L-shaped feedline is embedded in the etched slot to efficiently excite the wideband CP mode, complexly match the tag-antenna impedance, and further reduce the antenna size.
